# AI Continuity Log

Date: 2026-03-14

## Purpose

This file is the append-only memory ledger for `AURA Node Studio`.

It exists so future Codex sessions do not need to rediscover the whole project from scratch.
It should accumulate project context over time.

## Instruction To Future AI Sessions

Read this file before doing substantial work.
Then append a new entry after every single reply.

Rules:
- append only
- do not delete old content
- do not rewrite old entries unless the user explicitly asks
- record both technical work and important discussion decisions
- if the user corrects the project framing, record the correction
- if no code or file changes happen, record that clearly
- include concrete references to files and important logic locations whenever relevant
- if a large code generation step happens, list the generated files and what each one contains

## Entry Format

Use this structure for each new entry:

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM
- `User Intent:`
- `Discussion Summary:`
- `Actions Taken:`
- `Files Touched:`
- `Reference Points:`
- `Decisions:`
- `Open Questions:`
- `Next Step:`

---

### Entry

- `Discussion Summary:` The correct clarification is that a brand-new board is not necessarily electrically blank. Many new boards ship with something already flashed in main flash for factory test, demo behavior, or stock firmware, and the chip itself also contains built-in ROM boot code. However, strong heating on a brand-new board can also come from board-level hardware behavior such as a regulator issue or a fault, so the explanation should not rely only on preloaded firmware.
- `Actions Taken:` No project files were changed beyond this continuity entry. Prepared a direct explanation distinguishing factory-programmed content from hardware-level heat causes.

For Windows serial detection, `pnputil` is more reliable in this environment than `Get-CimInstance` or `Get-PnpDevice`, both of which returned access-denied errors in the current shell.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-17 10:23:44
- `User Intent:` Upgrade the earlier detector into a complete one-shot script that can detect boards and expose their available specs in one run instead of adding more stepwise helper files.
- `Discussion Summary:` The earlier lightweight serial-port tool was expanded into a fuller board inspection utility. The upgraded script now combines `pnputil` port enumeration, live port detection through `.NET` serial APIs, registry-backed device metadata from `HKLM:\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Enum\...`, VID/PID/REV parsing, bridge-chip classification, likely board-family guesses, manufacturer/vendor extraction, driver and service reporting, location strings, serial-style instance suffixes, and notes for Bluetooth or generic devices. The tool also now supports `-Detailed`, `-Port`, and `-Json` modes in addition to the earlier connected-only, include-disconnected, and watch modes.
- `Actions Taken:` Reworked `local_tools/windows/list_serial_boards.ps1` to add registry-safe metadata extraction, USB ID parsing, bridge-chip detection, vendor inference, single-port filtering, and detailed output. Updated `local_tools/windows/README.md` to document the new fields and commands. Fixed two PowerShell strict-mode bugs uncovered during validation: one parser issue from inline conditional expressions inside an array literal, and one missing-property issue for optional registry fields like `BusReportedDeviceDesc`. Also normalized the display path so detailed output works for a single matching object as well as multiple results. Verified the finished script by running default mode, `-IncludeDisconnected`, `-IncludeDisconnected -Port COM11 -Detailed`, `-IncludeDisconnected -Port COM4 -Detailed`, and `-IncludeDisconnected -Json`.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`, `local_tools/windows/list_serial_boards.ps1`, `local_tools/windows/README.md`
- `Reference Points:` `local_tools/windows/list_serial_boards.ps1` now includes the added logic blocks `Normalize-PortFilter`, `Get-OptionalPropertyValue`, `Get-RegistryDeviceInfo`, `Get-UsbIdData`, `Get-VendorGuess`, `Get-BridgeChip`, `Get-SerialId`, and `Get-Notes`, in addition to the earlier scan functions. `local_tools/windows/README.md` now documents the expanded capability set and the `-Detailed` and `-Port` usage patterns.
- `Decisions:` Keep one script as the main reusable Windows board inspector instead of splitting the functionality across multiple smaller files. Use registry-backed enrichment because it exposes materially more board and USB detail than `pnputil` output alone in this environment.
- `Open Questions:` Windows still cannot guarantee an exact retail board name for generic USB serial devices. For example, `COM11` can now be narrowed to a `CH9102/CH910x`-based board and likely `ESP32`/`ESP8266` family, but not to a precise board SKU without the device being actively connected or presenting a more specific descriptor.
- `Next Step:` Use `local_tools/windows/list_serial_boards.ps1 -Watch` while plugging boards in and out to confirm real-time port mapping, then rely on `-Port COMx -Detailed` whenever the user wants the full spec block for one specific board.

The AO3407 arrangement is appropriate for switching only the `LED/BLK` backlight pin, not the display's main `VCC`. The described component values are sensible: source at `3.3V`, drain to `LED/BLK`, gate driven from the ESP32 through about `150 ohm`, and `100k` from gate to source for a default-off state. The answer should also note the active-low behavior and remind the user that this assumes the display module already includes the backlight current-limiting components that most ST7735 breakout boards have.
- `Actions Taken:` No product files were changed in this step apart from the continuity log. Prepared a practical clarification response focused on the user's exact AO3407 wiring and the separation between TFT `VCC` and `LED/BLK`.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` Current firmware backlight config remains in `apps/aura_host/include/tft_display_config.h`, with `GPIO21` assigned for backlight control and active-low behavior intended for the AO3407 path.
- `Decisions:` Advise powering the TFT logic directly from ESP32 `3.3V` and using the AO3407 only on the backlight pin, not on the full display supply rail.
- `Open Questions:` Whether the specific TFT board has an onboard resistor/transistor network on `LED/BLK`, although most common `1.8 inch ST7735` breakouts do.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-17 21:57:06
- `User Intent:` Confirm whether sharing the SPI pins between the TFT and the nRF24L01 will cause them to disturb each other.
- `Discussion Summary:` The answer should reassure the user that shared SPI is the standard and correct hardware approach here, not a compromise, as long as the devices have separate chip-select control and the inactive device is properly deselected. The main practical risks are not SPI sharing itself but poor radio power decoupling, incorrect chip-select handling, long noisy jumper wires, or leaving both devices selected at the same time. The response should also mention that the TFT generally only uses `SCK` and `MOSI`, while the nRF24 also uses `MISO`, so there is no inherent conflict when the TFT is idle.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-17 22:00:04
- `User Intent:` Ask whether the ESP32 can handle fast changing display values while the incoming count data is arriving from the nRF24L01 over the same shared SPI bus.
- `Discussion Summary:` The correct answer is that the display and radio cannot use the same SPI bus at the exact same instant, but they can still work together effectively by time-sharing the bus in very short bursts. In practice this is usually fine for a remote UI, because nRF24 transfers are small and the user only needs the displayed number to update at a human-visible rate. The main risk appears when the firmware tries to do heavy TFT transfers, especially full-screen writes, while also expecting to service a high rate of radio packets. The right design guidance is to decouple acquisition from rendering: keep receiving radio updates quickly into RAM, and render only the changed digits or a limited refresh rate such as 20-60 Hz. If event rate becomes very high, the node should send aggregated counts or deltas rather than one radio packet per event.
- `Actions Taken:` No code changes were made in this step apart from the continuity log. Prepared an architecture answer centered on SPI bus time-sharing, event buffering, partial redraws, and practical display refresh strategy.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` The current TFT renderer already contains buffered and partial-redraw logic in `apps/aura_host/src/tft_ui.cpp`, which is relevant because minimizing display transfer time is the key to making shared SPI with the nRF24L01 behave well under fast updates.
- `Decisions:` Keep the shared SPI bus plan. Recommend software scheduling and buffered updates rather than adding a second SPI bus unless actual throughput testing proves it necessary.
- `Open Questions:` What the user means by `counting fast`: tens of updates per second, hundreds per second, or true pulse-level event counting. The required strategy depends on that rate.
- `Next Step:` Explain that effective concurrency is achievable on shared SPI, then recommend the correct firmware pattern: receive fast, buffer, and redraw only the necessary digits at a capped UI rate.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-17 22:03:41
- `User Intent:` Ask for a calculated worst-case answer on whether the nRF24L01 and TFT can collide under the current shared-SPI design, because the remote is still at the hardwiring stage and the user wants to know the real limits before committing.
- `Discussion Summary:` The key limit is not basic electrical sharing, which is standard and fine, but service latency. The current TFT driver uses `16 MHz` SPI in `apps/aura_host/src/tft_ui.cpp`, and a full-screen push for the rotated `160 x 128` view transfers `160 * 128 * 2 = 40,960 bytes`, which is about `20.48 ms` of raw SPI time before software overhead. The nRF24L01 spec states up to `2 Mbps` air data rate, a `4-pin hardware SPI` host interface with `max 8 Mbps`, and `3 separate 32-byte TX and RX FIFOs`. Because the RX FIFO is only three packets deep, if the host spends about `20.5 ms` doing one blocking full-frame TFT transfer, any sustained radio traffic above roughly `3 / 0.02048 Ōēł 146 packets/s` can overflow the radio FIFO before the MCU gets back to drain it. That means yes, there are real conditions where the current shared-SPI design can lose radio packets during display activity. Importantly, this is not only a shared-bus problem: even a separate SPI bus would still be at risk if the firmware remains blocking for 20 ms at a time. The safer design for fast counts is to keep radio packets aggregated, update only a small digit region on the TFT, cap visible UI refresh rate, and optionally bring out the nRF24 `IRQ` pin for future lower-latency receive handling.
- `Actions Taken:` Re-read the current project timing assumptions and the TFT driver constants. Calculated the current full-frame SPI transfer time from the local firmware using the configured `16 MHz` bus speed and the rotated screen dimensions. Cross-checked the nRF24L01 capability limits from the Nordic product specification, including `2 Mbps` on-air data rate, `max 8 Mbps` host SPI, `3 separate 32-byte TX and RX FIFOs`, and the packet timing/130 us turnaround information. No code changes were made in this step apart from the continuity log.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` TFT SPI speed is set at `apps/aura_host/src/tft_ui.cpp:32` in `kSpiSettings(16000000, ...)`. Full-frame TFT transfer path is in `apps/aura_host/src/tft_ui.cpp:305` and `apps/aura_host/src/tft_ui.cpp:386` under `present()` and `presentRect()`. Screen buffer dimensions are tied to `apps/aura_host/src/tft_ui.cpp:549-557`. nRF24L01 capability references used for the calculation come from the Nordic product specification hosted on DevZone, especially the feature summary showing `max 8Mbps` SPI and `3 separate 32 bytes TX and RX FIFOs`, and the timing section covering `2Mbps` air rate and `130us` turnaround timing.
- `Decisions:` Keep shared SPI as acceptable for normal AURA menu/radio use, but explicitly acknowledge that it is not collision-proof under sustained high packet rates combined with blocking full-screen TFT writes. If the user expects true high-rate counter streaming, recommend protocol aggregation and small display updates first; only consider alternate wiring if that use case is central.
- `Open Questions:` Whether the user's future `counting fast` use case is closer to `tens of packets per second`, `hundreds`, or true event streaming. Also whether the user wants to reserve one more pin now for `nRF24 IRQ`, which would improve future receive responsiveness.
- `Next Step:` Give the user the concrete threshold numbers and recommend the wiring choice: keep shared SPI for the normal AURA remote, but if the design must tolerate sustained high packet-rate telemetry, reserve the `IRQ` pin now and avoid protocols that send one packet per event.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-18 09:39:18
- `User Intent:` Understand what a `.bat` file is in practical Windows terms, using the current `AURA Host` upload and monitor launchers as examples.
- `Discussion Summary:` The explanation needed to stay basic and concrete. A `.bat` file is a Windows batch script: a plain text file containing command-line instructions that Windows executes in order when the file is run. In this repo, the `.bat` files are not doing firmware logic themselves; they are just convenience launchers that call PowerShell and forward to `apps/aura_host/tools/run_pio.ps1` with an action such as `upload` or `monitor`, then keep the terminal window open with `pause` so the output can be read.
- `Actions Taken:` Re-read `apps/aura_host/UPLOAD_AURA_HOST.bat` and `apps/aura_host/OPEN_SERIAL_MONITOR.bat` to explain them line by line. No project code or workflow files were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` `apps/aura_host/UPLOAD_AURA_HOST.bat` calls `powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File "%~dp0tools\run_pio.ps1" -Action upload`, optionally with a passed `COM` port. `apps/aura_host/OPEN_SERIAL_MONITOR.bat` does the same with `-Action monitor`. The real work still happens in `apps/aura_host/tools/run_pio.ps1`.
- `Decisions:` Keep teaching the user by mapping simple wrapper files back to the real script and command underneath.
- `Open Questions:` Whether the user wants the next explanation to cover batch-file syntax symbols like `%~dp0`, `%1`, `@echo off`, and `pause`.
- `Next Step:` Explain the current `.bat` files in plain language and, if needed, break down each batch-script token one by one.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-18 12:08:31
- `User Intent:` Validate whether the planned parser can handle different accents accurately enough for instant spoken item recognition without user repetition in real customer-facing shop contexts.
- `Discussion Summary:` The critical clarification is that accent robustness is primarily an ASR (speech-to-text) problem, not a parser problem. A parser can map recognized text to intent/entity, but it cannot recover words that ASR mishears. The right guidance is to optimize the voice pipeline for high recall and low-friction correction: strong ASR engine choice, domain phrase biasing, alias dictionaries, fuzzy/entity matching against catalog, confidence thresholds, and low-friction clarification flows only when confidence is low.
- `Actions Taken:` No code or config files were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`

- `Open Questions:` Which target languages/accents are required first, whether cloud ASR is acceptable, and acceptable median recognition latency at checkout/in-clinic usage points.
- `Next Step:` Define the speech stack requirements: language/accent coverage, latency budget, confidence handling policy, and catalog alias strategy before selecting implementation tooling.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-18 13:40:39
- `User Intent:` Decide which MCU should be used for an AURA locator node from the already-available ATTiny parts (`402`, `204`, `404`, `416`).
- `Discussion Summary:` The recommendation needs to be based on the real node role rather than only part availability. For an AURA node that will likely need an nRF24L01 radio, a few outputs for locate feedback, and some growth room, `ATtiny416` is the strongest choice among the listed options because it provides the most GPIO headroom while keeping the same small-AVR family. `ATtiny404` is the minimum reasonable fallback for a very small node. `ATtiny402` and `ATtiny204` are too constrained for a comfortable first node unless the design is extremely minimal. A key caveat is that all of these remain small-memory MCUs, so firmware discipline matters; heavy frameworks or bloated radio stacks will not fit comfortably.
- `Actions Taken:` No source files or firmware were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` Node recommendation is being made against the current host/locator project direction in `README.md` and the existing host-side radio/UI flow already present in `host_remote/src/input_actions.cpp`, `host_remote/src/radio_self_test.cpp`, and `host_remote/src/tft_ui.cpp`.
- `Decisions:` Frame the MCU recommendation around a practical node prototype path: prefer `ATtiny416`, accept `ATtiny404` for a reduced node, avoid starting with `402` or `204`.
- `Open Questions:` Exact node scope is still unfrozen: number of outputs, whether a buzzer or sensor will be included, and whether the node firmware will be written bare-metal/lean AVR style or through a higher-overhead abstraction layer.
- `Next Step:` Freeze the node responsibility set first, then map pins and memory budget around the chosen MCU before writing node firmware.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-18 14:05:49
- `User Intent:` For the temporary Arduino Nano based node, ask for the practical wiring of a `WS2812` LED strip together with an `nRF24L01`.
- `Discussion Summary:` The response needs to focus on safe prototype wiring, especially the power domain mismatch: Nano and WS2812 are typically `5V`, while `nRF24L01` must stay on a stable `3.3V` rail. The key point to emphasize is that the radio should not be powered directly from a weak onboard `3.3V` pin if current spikes are expected; an external `3.3V` regulator with local capacitors is the safer wiring.
- `Actions Taken:` No code or design files were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` This discussion is for the temporary node prototype path and not yet tied to a committed node firmware source file. Existing host-side radio expectations remain in `host_remote/src/radio_self_test.cpp`.
- `Decisions:` Keep the answer practical and wiring-first rather than trying to formalize node firmware before the prototype hardware is assembled.
- `Open Questions:` Exact LED count on the WS2812 strip and whether the user will power the strip from USB or an external `5V` supply.
- `Next Step:` Build the Nano prototype with correct shared ground, protected WS2812 data line, and a stable dedicated `3.3V` rail for the radio, then test radio stability before writing node behavior.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-18 14:19:42
- `User Intent:` Ask for the wiring of a simpler node using `ATtiny404` and a single RGB LED.
- `Discussion Summary:` The useful interpretation is an `ATtiny404 + nRF24L01 + one discrete RGB LED` node. The recommended mapping keeps programming access intact on `PA0/UPDI`, uses the default SPI pins on `PA1` to `PA4` for the radio, uses `PA5` for `CE`, and uses `PB2`, `PB1`, and `PB0` for the RGB LED channels because those are the cleanest output trio on the 14-pin package.

- `Discussion Summary:` This is expected hot-plug behavior for this setup, not a surprising firmware-only fault. The radio is initialized once in `setup()`, and the current receiver code does not attempt runtime recovery if the module disappears and returns. Hot insertion can also leave the radio and SPI bus in an undefined state because `nRF24L01` modules are not intended to be unplugged and replugged live in normal operation.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-19 18:49:10
- `User Intent:` Understand whether powering an Arduino Nano from a cheap USB power bank, then using the Nano's `3.3V` pin for the `nRF24L01`, is stable enough or whether a battery or different power source is needed.
- `Discussion Summary:` The key issue is not mainly that power banks are "noisy"; it is that many Nano boards have a weak `3.3V` rail for radio burst current, and `nRF24L01` modules are sensitive to local supply dips and wiring inductance. A USB power bank can be acceptable for the Nano itself, but the radio often benefits from dedicated decoupling and sometimes a separate `3.3V` regulator, especially for higher-power modules.
- `Actions Taken:` No code or design files were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` This guidance applies to the current Nano transmitter prototype with `nRF24L01` on `D9/D10` CE/CSN and the general AURA node bring-up path using low-cost radio modules.
- `Decisions:` Emphasize that the Nano USB power source can be fine, but the Nano `3.3V` pin should not be trusted blindly for radio stability.
- `Open Questions:` Which exact Nano variant the user has and whether the radio module is the small PCB version or a PA/LNA amplified version.
- `Next Step:` Recommend the practical power rule set for Nano plus `nRF24L01`, including local capacitors and when to use a separate `3.3V` regulator.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-19 18:52:30
- `User Intent:` Ask for the exact burst current of the `nRF24L01+` that can cause the MCU to reset.
- `Discussion Summary:` The correct explanation is that there is no single universal reset current. The radio's own current is specified, but whether the MCU resets depends on supply droop and the MCU brown-out threshold. The answer should therefore distinguish between normal `nRF24L01+` current draw and the voltage-drop mechanism that actually causes resets.
- `Actions Taken:` Looked up current-consumption and brown-out figures from the `nRF24L01` product specification and the `ATtiny202/204/402/404/406` BOD/POR characteristics. No project source files were changed beyond appending this continuity entry.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` Relevant figures are `nRF24L01` TX current around `11.3 mA` at `0 dBm`, plus the `ATtiny404` BOD levels around `1.8 V`, `2.6 V`, and `4.2 V`, which determine how much droop margin exists from a `3.3V` rail.
- `Decisions:` Answer with the mechanism, not a misleading single-number claim.
- `Open Questions:` Whether the user's module is a plain `nRF24L01+` board or a PA/LNA amplified version, which would change the current range substantially.
- `Next Step:` Explain the current numbers, the brown-out thresholds, and how to estimate reset risk from supply impedance.

Those requirements align more closely with the prior AURA deterministic component-builder approach than with a display-graphics tool.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-21 09:29
- `User Intent:` Decide whether the circuit creator UI in this version should use a simple black-and-white pixel-graphics style for ease of creation and a strong look, while avoiding looking like a copy of the `Nothing` brand.
- `Discussion Summary:` The proposed direction is sound for V1 if it is treated as AURA's own restrained visual language rather than a direct `Nothing` imitation. A monochrome pixel-based style fits deterministic tools, low-noise hardware UI, and easier asset production. The main caution is that full-scene pixel styling can make dense editor workflows feel toy-like or harder to read if text, forms, and precision controls are rendered too crudely. The best approach is a hybrid: pixel language for icons, markers, mini-illustrations, empty states, grids, and selection chrome; cleaner non-pixel typography and structured panels for editing-heavy surfaces.
- `Actions Taken:` No product source files were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry. Prepared a design recommendation focused on visual direction and usability tradeoffs for the future circuit creator/editor.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`
- `Reference Points:` This decision is conceptually tied to the future deterministic component/circuit editor direction previously referenced through `../AURA_ui_core/README.md`, `../AURA_ui_core/docs/PROJECT_GOAL.md`, and `../AURA_2_0/src/main.js`, but no implementation files were edited in this turn.
- `Decisions:` Support a black-and-white V1 visual system, but avoid making the entire editor depend on coarse pixel rendering. Recommend keeping the branding original and restrained rather than echoing the `Nothing` aesthetic too closely.
- `Open Questions:` Whether the user wants the circuit creator to lean more toward terminal/pixel-tool aesthetics or toward a cleaner CAD-like mono editor with only light pixel accents.
- `Next Step:` If requested, define the exact V1 visual rules for the circuit creator: typography, icon style, grid, panel chrome, node/pin visuals, and selection states.

### Entry
- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-21 16:15
- `User Intent:` Understand how upload should be done in practice now, whether to use the `.bat` wrappers or direct `pio` commands, and how PlatformIO knows which project or code to upload when many folders or files exist.
- `Discussion Summary:` The key clarification is that PlatformIO uploads a project build, not an individual source file. Which project it uses depends mainly on the current working directory or an explicitly provided project path. If the user runs `pio run -t upload` inside `host_remote/tests/blink_probe/`, PlatformIO uses that folder's `platformio.ini` and compiles the whole `src/` set for that project. If the user is in a different folder, then that other folder's `platformio.ini` becomes the active project unless `-d <path>` is used. The `.bat` wrappers are therefore just convenience launchers tied to one specific test project, while the direct `pio` commands are shorter but depend more on the current folder.
- `Actions Taken:` No project source files were changed in this turn beyond appending this continuity entry. Prepared a practical explanation contrasting project selection by current directory, explicit path, and local wrappers.

- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-22 16:01
- `User Intent:` Fix the remaining wire-snap bias so, when wiring between differently pitched packages, the snap prefers the component currently near the cursor instead of over-favoring the source-side package where the wire started.
- `Discussion Summary:` After the broader geometry-alignment layer was added, the user found the next real ergonomics bug: on a large-pin-pitch IC wired toward a smaller-pin-pitch IC, the start-side anchor logic could still dominate because orthogonal assist ran before the wider geometry pass. That meant the source package could continue pulling the draft target even after the cursor had moved close to the destination package. The correct fix was not just another tolerance tweak, but a priority layer that first asks which package is actually nearest the cursor and lets that package's pin/edge geometry have first claim on the active snap.
- `Actions Taken:` Updated `studio_ui/src/components/Canvas.tsx` to add `getDistanceToBounds()` and `getPriorityWireAlignmentCandidates()`, which locate the nearest component body to the current wire cursor and collect only that nearby package's edges, centers, and pins as preferred snap candidates. Updated active wire snap resolution so it now checks those priority candidates first, using the cursor's direct snapped position, before falling back to the older start-side orthogonal assist and then the broader global guide set. This preserves the right-angle helper, but stops it from overpowering the destination package when the cursor is clearly operating near that package instead. Ran `studio_ui> npm.cmd run lint`, and it passed successfully.
- `Files Touched:` `AI_CONTINUITY_LOG.md`, `studio_ui/src/components/Canvas.tsx`

- `Decisions:` Keep start-side orthogonal assist as a fallback because it is still useful for clean wire shaping, but stop treating it as the dominant force when the cursor is close to a different package. Use nearest-component proximity rather than package size or pin-count heuristics so large and small packages behave consistently.

- `Timestamp:` 2026-03-22 16:47
- `User Intent:` Fix the still-visible Vite overlay after the TypeScript error was resolved.

- `Discussion Summary:` The user proposed the correct general direction: light behavior should not be hardcoded as a special-case LED mechanic first. Instead, the creator should let the author either select an existing internal shape/actor from the component or create a simple helper shape such as a circle, rectangle, or curve, then attach light-related behavior to that target. The user also clarified an important semantic split: brightness can be represented primarily through transparency/opacity, while color should be a separate property only when the component concept actually supports color variation, such as RGB LEDs. For a normal LED, the placed component should typically have one authored display color chosen at creation/placement time and only vary intensity; for RGB-capable parts, color may later become a real runtime-changing property driven by logic or firmware.
- `Actions Taken:` No product code changes were made in this turn. Captured the behavior-authoring direction in continuity so the next creator-side implementation can follow this model rather than improvising LED-specific behavior logic.

- `Decisions:` Treat light behavior as target-based component authoring, not as a one-off LED feature. Separate `base authored color` from `runtime-varying brightness`, and only introduce `runtime-varying color` for components whose real behavior justifies it, such as RGB indicators.

- `Next Step:` Define the first creator-side light behavior model around target selection, base fill color, opacity/brightness mapping, optional glow overlay, and a future capability flag for color-varying parts.

FigmaŌĆÖs ellipse/line/arc model, PowerPointŌĆÖs curve/path workflow, and draw.ioŌĆÖs support for basic primitives and freehand/custom shapes all support that direction. Instead, child anchors are preserved in absolute stage space and converted into the new base-relative coordinate system when needed, and only autogenerated base-detail layers (those with `generated_` IDs) are replaced. Added `getRenderedChildLayers()` so child rendering now derives final absolute shape layers deterministically. Replaced the old mixed translated-group child render path with direct rendering of absolute child layers. - `Timestamp:` 2026-03-23 23:56
- `User Intent:` Fix a creator drawing bug before any further expansion: when a shape tool was selected, a single tap on the stage was immediately creating a tiny/extreme shape, while double-tap/drag behavior felt like the only usable way to draw properly.
- `Discussion Summary:` The userÆs diagnosis matched the implementation. Creator was committing a new shape on every pointer-up while in draw mode, even when there had been no meaningful drag between pointer-down and pointer-up. Because many shape tools normalize or clamp tiny bounds, a simple click could still produce a minimal-size shape, which felt like a bug. The correct fix was not to special-case one shape type but to enforce a real draw-gesture threshold before committing any tool-created sketch layer.
- `Actions Taken:` Updated `studio_ui/src/components/ComponentCreatorWorkspace.tsx` to add `hasMeaningfulDrawGesture()`, which checks whether a draw interaction actually moved far enough to count as an intentional shape creation. For line tools it uses an 8px distance threshold; for area-based tools it requires at least 8px of width or height delta. Updated `handleStagePointerUp()` so draw-mode now commits a shape only when that threshold is met; otherwise it exits draw mode without creating a layer. Rather than adding more shell clutter, the work was wired into the same update path used by drag, resize, and inspector edits so relationships are not just cosmetic metadata. The result is a first real creator relationship model: line layers can now follow another line as `parallel` or `perpendicular`, non-line shapes can align to another shape by `same x`, `same y`, or `same center`, and saved dimension guides can persist on the stage instead of disappearing when selection changes.

Added geometric helpers `getShapeCenter()`, `applyLineRelation()`, and `applyShapeRelation()`, then replaced the old isolated constraint enforcement with `applyShapeConstraints(shape, allShapes)` and `resolveShapeConstraints(shapes)` so creator can re-resolve relations across the whole sketch after updates. Wired this into the real edit flow by updating shape move, resize, trim, split, draw-commit, and selected-shape inspector edits to use `resolveShapeConstraints()` via the new `commitShapeLayerUpdate()` / `updateSelectedShape()` helpers. Added persistent dimension rendering through `getDimensionLabel()` and `renderPersistentDimension()`, plus a creator-side `persistentDimensions` state list. The selected-shape inspector now exposes `Save width / height` for non-line shapes and `Save length / dx / dy` for lines, and saved guides can also be removed directly in the inspector. Added new `Relations` controls in the selected-shape inspector: lines now support choosing another line target plus `free / parallel / perpendicular`, while non-line shapes support another shape target plus `free / same x / same y / center`. The stage now renders all saved dimensions whenever the `Dims` overlay is on, while still keeping the transient selected-shape/base guides. Deleting a shape now also removes any saved dimensions attached to it and clears relation references from remaining shapes that targeted it. - `Next Step:` Commit and push this cleanup, then decide whether to continue by trimming draft-related circuit-store state out of `Circuit Studio` or by wiring the new `shared/contracts_v1/` schemas into the first concrete host/phone-side data-loading path.
